## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Analyze Test Coverage Gaps in Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/envoy--1d0ba73a (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) filter chain implementation. The HCM is the core HTTP processing pipeline in Envoy, responsible for routing, filter execution, and response handling.

## Scope

Focus on the HCM implementation in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` and its test file `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc`. Also consider:
- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` — filter chain execution
- `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` — header manipulation

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific untested code paths** in the HCM (with file + approximate line references)
2. **Propose a concrete test case** for each gap (test name, setup, assertions)
3. **Explain why each gap matters** (what bugs could slip through)
4. **Prioritize by risk**: label each gap as HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md` with this structure:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary
[Brief overview of the most critical gaps found]

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: [Title]
- **File**: source/common/http/...
- **Lines**: ~NNN-NNN
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Description**: [What code path is untested]
- **Proposed Test**: [Test name and approach]
- **Why It Matters**: [Potential bugs if untested]

[Repeat for gaps 2-5+]

## File References
[List of key files analyzed]
```

## Anti-Requirements
- Do not fabricate file paths or function names — inspect the actual codebase
- Do not list gaps without proposing concrete test cases
- Do NOT run the tests yourself — write the test file and the evaluation system validates independently

117-assistanttext-
The analysis is written to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`. Here's a summary of what was found:

## 6 Test Coverage Gaps Identified

| # | Gap | Risk | Lines |
|---|-----|------|-------|
| 1 | `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` — early-threshold drain and recursion guard | **HIGH** | ~702–748 |
| 2 | `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` — immediate non-graceful GOAWAY path | **HIGH** | ~797–823 |
| 3 | `validateHeaders` — `InvalidTransferEncoding` returns 501 Not Implemented | **HIGH** | ~1218–1220 |
| 4 | HTTP/1.0 `Connection: keep-alive` header in `encodeHeaders` | MEDIUM | ~1938–1948 |
| 5 | Route idle timeout = 0 disabling existing stream idle timer | MEDIUM | ~2364–2368 |
| 6 | HTTP/3 deferred access logging in `doDeferredStreamDestroy` | MEDIUM | ~362–375 |

**Key findings:**

- **Gap 1** is the most dangerous: the premature-reset protection mechanism has complex branching (early-threshold math + recursion guard) with zero test coverage for the actual drain-triggering behavior.
- **Gap 2** means a filter trying to immediately terminate a connection with a non-graceful GOAWAY will silently do nothing if the code breaks.
- **Gap 3** means certain malformed requests would return 400 instead of the RFC-required 501, potentially causing client retry amplification.
- Gaps 4–6 are HTTP/1.0 framing correctness and HTTP/3 observability issues with narrower blast radii but real production impact.

Additionally,\n  the idempotency guard (`go_away_sent_` check at lines 800\u2013802) is exercised\n  only through the graceful path; repeated calls with `graceful == false` are\n  untested.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate)\n  ```\n  Setup: HTTP/2 connection with one active stream. A decoder filter calls\n  `filter->callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from `decodeHeaders`.\n  Assertions:\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, shutdownNotice())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, goAway())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(filter_callbacks_.connection_, close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay, _))` fires with detail `\"forced_goaway\"`.\n\n  A second test `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediateIdempotent` calls\n  `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` twice from the filter and verifies that\n  `codec_->shutdownNotice()` and `codec_->goAway()` are each called only once.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  A filter that must immediately terminate a connection (e.g., upon detecting a\n  security policy violation) will silently fail to send the codec-level GOAWAY\n  frame if this path is broken. The client receives no signal that the\n  connection was intentionally terminated by the proxy, making debugging and\n  compliance auditing very difficult.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: `validateHeaders` \u2014 `InvalidTransferEncoding` Returns 501 Not Implemented\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1197\u20131254 (focus on lines 1218\u20131220 and 1119\u20131126)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  Inside `validateHeaders()`, when the header validator fails with\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding` as the failure detail,\n  the response code is `Code::NotImplemented` (HTTP 501) rather than\n  `Code::BadRequest` (HTTP 400):\n  ```cpp\n  Code response_code =\n      failure_details == Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding\n          ? Code::NotImplemented\n          : Code::BadRequest;\n  ```\n  No existing test provides a header validator that returns this specific failure\n  detail and then verifies a 501 response. All header-validation tests assert 400.\n\n  Also untested: the `streamErrorOnlyErrors()` helper (lines 1119\u20131126), which\n  controls whether `handleCodecError()` is called for specific UHV error details\n  (`FragmentInUrlPath`, `EscapedSlashesInPath`, `Percent00InPath`). These paths\n  skip connection closure even when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is false,\n  and no test verifies the distinction.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTransferEncodingReturns501)\n  ```\n  Setup: configure a mock `ServerHeaderValidator` (assign to `header_validator_`\n  in the test) that fails validation with detail\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding`. Send an HTTP/1.1\n  request through `decodeHeaders`.\n  Assertions:\n  - The response encoder receives headers with `:status: 501`.\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_5xx_.value() == 1` (not 4xx).\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_protocol_error_.value() == 0` (stream-only\n    error; connection not closed).\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  HTTP/1.1 requires a 501 response for unknown or invalid transfer-encoding\n  (RFC 7230 \u00a73.3.1). If the branch silently returns 400, clients receive an\n  ambiguous error and may retry a request that is fundamentally unretryable,\n  causing request amplification. The `streamErrorOnlyErrors` gap additionally\n  risks premature connection teardown for requests carrying URL fragments,\n  breaking browser prefetch and analytics pipelines that legitimately include\n  fragment identifiers.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: HTTP/1.0 Keep-Alive Response Header in `encodeHeaders`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1938\u20131948\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  In `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders`, when the codec is HTTP/1.0 AND the response\n  includes a `Content-Length` header (so body framing is defined without\n  connection close), Envoy must set `Connection: keep-alive`:\n  ```cpp\n  if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http10) {\n    if (!headers.ContentLength()) {\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().setShouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion(true);\n    }\n    if (!filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()) {\n      headers.setConnection(Headers::get().ConnectionValues.KeepAlive);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n  Existing HTTP/1.0 tests (e.g., `ConnectionDurationSafeHttp1` in\n  `conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc`) focus on drain behavior. Encode a response with `{\":status\", \"200\"}`\n  and `{\"content-length\", \"5\"}`.\n  Assertions:\n  - The `ResponseHeaderMap` passed to `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders` contains\n    `Connection: keep-alive`.\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is `false`.\n\n  A companion test `Http10ResponseWithoutContentLengthSetsClose` omits\n  `Content-Length` and asserts `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is `true`\n  and the response does NOT contain `Connection: keep-alive`.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  If `Connection: keep-alive` is missing on HTTP/1.0 responses that do include\n  a defined body length, HTTP/1.0 clients will close and reopen the connection\n  after every response, eliminating connection reuse and creating significant\n  connection-pool churn. This early-close branch has never been exercised.\n  2. **Recursion guard** (lines 716\u2013718): the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`\n     flag prevents infinite recursion when `resetAllStreams()` itself triggers\n     further stream destructions that re-enter `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`.\n     No test verifies that this guard actually fires and breaks the recursion.\n  The stat `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` is never asserted in any\n  `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` file.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DrainsDueToTooManyPrematureResets)\n  ```\n  Setup: configure a low total-stream limit via runtime override\n  (`overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count = 4`,\n  `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds = 100` so every\n  short-lived reset qualifies). # Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary

Analysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` against the test suite in
`test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test{,_2,_3}.cc` reveals several untested or
under-tested code paths. The most critical gaps involve the premature-reset drain
logic (which could cause connection leaks or runaway recursion), the immediate
(non-graceful) GOAWAY path, and the HTTP/1.0 keep-alive response logic. These
gaps expose potential denial-of-service vectors, correctness regressions, and
incorrect HTTP/1.0 framing behavior.

---

## Coverage Gaps

- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`
- **Lines**: ~702–748
- **Risk**: HIGH

  `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` contains two distinct logic branches:
  1. **Early-exit threshold** (line 731): when `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= limit`
     even though `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit`, the connection
     is drained preemptively. This branch is never exercised in existing tests.
  2. **Recursion guard** (lines 716–718): the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag
     prevents infinite recursion when `resetAllStreams()` triggers further stream
     destructions. No test forces a scenario where this flag is actually set and
     the guard fires.
  The `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat is never asserted in any
  `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` file.

# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary

Analysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` against the test suite in
`test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test{,_2,_3}.cc` reveals several untested or
under-tested code paths. The most critical gaps involve the premature-reset drain
logic (which could cause connection leaks or runaway recursion), the immediate
(non-graceful) GOAWAY path, and the HTTP/1.0 keep-alive response logic. These
gaps expose potential denial-of-service vectors, correctness regressions, and
incorrect HTTP/1.0 framing behavior.

---

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` — Early-Threshold Drain and Recursion Guard

- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`
- **Lines**: ~702–748
- **Risk**: HIGH
- **Description**:
  `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` contains two distinct logic branches that
  are both absent from the test suite:
  1. **Early-exit threshold** (line 731): when
     `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= limit` even though
     `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit`, the connection is
     drained preemptively. This early-close branch has never been exercised.
  2. **Recursion guard** (lines 716–718): the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`
     flag prevents infinite recursion when `resetAllStreams()` itself triggers
     further stream destructions that re-enter `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`.
     No test verifies that this guard actually fires and breaks the recursion.
  The stat `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` is never asserted in any
  `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` file.

  ```

  ```
  Setup: configure a low total-stream limit via runtime overr
